  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_11b7d5cb-9477-4302-bb8e-a0a1c19ab886'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer2302191355425952171">All of Waylander's instincts had screamed at him to spurn the contract from Kaem the cruel, the killer of nations. But he had ignored them. He had made his kill.   <span id="freeText2302191355425952171" style="display:none">All of Waylander's instincts had screamed at him to spurn the contract from Kaem the cruel, the killer of nations. But he had ignored them. He had made his kill. And even as he went to collect his gold, he knew that he had been betrayed.<br />Now the Dark Brotherhood and the hounds of chaos were hunting him, even as Kaem's armies waged war on the Drenai lands, intent on killing every man, woman, and child. The Drenai soldiers were doomed to ultimate defeat, and chaos would soon reign. <br />Then a strange old man told Waylander that the only way to turn the tide of battle would be for Waylander himself to retrieve the legendary Armor of Bronze from its hiding place deep within a shadow-haunted land. He would be hunted. He was certain to fail. But he must try, the old man commanded--commanded in the name of his son, the king, who had been slain by an assassin... <br />Waylander was the most unlikely of heroes--for he was a traitor, the Slayer who had killed the king...</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<div id="review_2336920559" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2336920559" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2336920559?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2336920559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4664122690079029889"><b>“Once I was a lamb, playing in a green field. then the wolves came. Now I am an eagle and I fly in a different universe.”</b><br/><br/>“Waylander” is the third instalment in the Drenai Saga if we look at the order in which books were written. According to the internal chronology of the cycle, this is <b>the opening volume of this epic tale</b>.<br/><br/>The book takes us hundreds of years before the events described in the “Legend”. The characters that had been considered legendary, even divine there, in “Waylander” take shap</span>
  <span id="freeText4664122690079029889" style="display:none"><b>“Once I was a lamb, playing in a green field. then the wolves came. Now I am an eagle and I fly in a different universe.”</b><br /><br />“Waylander” is the third instalment in the Drenai Saga if we look at the order in which books were written. According to the internal chronology of the cycle, this is <b>the opening volume of this epic tale</b>.<br /><br />The book takes us hundreds of years before the events described in the “Legend”. The characters that had been considered legendary, even divine there, in “Waylander” take shape and are shown as ordinary people with their personal problems and challenges.<br /><br />The main protagonist is a <b>soldier turned farmer turned assassin</b>. Typically for Mr Gemmell’s heroes, he is <b>shackled by his own past and whenever he tries to escape it, he sinks even further into the quagmires of fate</b>. We meet Waylander when he rescues a Source Priest tortured by a band of renegades. This good deed, first in a very long time in his career, has a domino effect and suddenly Waylander finds himself in the middle of the Drenai war of survival against Ventrian invaders. <br /><br />While what follows is <b>a classic Quest For A Magic Item (an armour to be precise) combined with yet another Hopeless Situation But Not All is Lost kind of setting</b> (war is nearly lost, morale is low and a miracle is needed to change this), Waylander is pleasant and fast read. <br /><br />It is a <b>fairly good, solid fantasy</b>. Mr Gemmell doesn’t get preachy and so you will not find paragraphs cut and paste from philosophy for dummies or self-help books. For such a short book, there is an incredible amount of action and it is nice to get to know the heroes we have only heard about before (like Karnak) or learn about the origins of things like The Thirty. <br /><br />On the other hand, “Waylander” is <b>hardly original</b>. Furthermore, the descriptions of battle scenes are rather cursory, as are the descriptions of secondary and tertiary protagonists. They tend to be poorly characterised, often with rather crude strokes what makes it difficult to get attached to them. <br /><br /><b>Gemmell Fandom does not need to be recommended, but even the outsiders should try the first volume of the Drenai Saga, because this is where everything had started.</b><br /><br />---<br />Also in The Drenai Saga: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577771334" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a> ★★★★★<br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305679740?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The King Beyond the Gate</a> ★★☆☆☆<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372503520" rel="nofollow noopener">Quest for Lost Heroes</a> ★★★★☆<br />5. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407425852" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Realm of the Wolf</a> ★★★☆☆<br />6. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2431984941?type=review#rating_170330840" rel="nofollow noopener">The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend</a> ★★★★☆<br />7. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2470949369" rel="nofollow noopener">The Legend of Deathwalker</a> ★★★★☆<br />8. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2517328446?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter Warriors</a> ★★★☆☆<br />9. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2621547766" rel="nofollow noopener">Hero in the Shadows</a> ★★★★★<br />10. White Wolf RTC<br />11. The Swords of Night and Day RTC</span>
  <a data-text-id="4664122690079029889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText4102784995083210838" style="display:none">Waylander (The Drenai Saga #3, Waylander #1), David Gemmell<br /><br />Waylander is a fantasy novel by British writer David Gemmell, published in 1986. <div id="review_1690592155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1690592155" />
    <a title="Paul O&#39;Neill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17331573-paul-o-neill"><img alt="Paul O&#39;Neill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462480730p2/17331573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1690592155?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul O&#39;Neill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul O&#39;Neill" href="/user/show/17331573-paul-o-neill">Paul O&#39;Neill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19041006-waylander">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1690592155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18054538510732682770">Another excellent story written by the master of fantasy. Modern fantasy owes a lot to David Gemmell, with many of today’s fantasy stars citing Gemmell as a major inspiration. And Waylander is a fantastic story which is compact (less than 400 pages) but nevertheless brimming with emotion.<br/><br/><b>Mini synopsis</b><br/>Waylander (lone-wolf, assassin and general kick-ass) saves a priest almost by accident which sets of a chain of world changing events. Waylander is set on an impossible mission and elsewhere, a majo</span>
  <span id="freeText18054538510732682770" style="display:none">Another excellent story written by the master of fantasy. Modern fantasy owes a lot to David Gemmell, with many of today’s fantasy stars citing Gemmell as a major inspiration. And Waylander is a fantastic story which is compact (less than 400 pages) but nevertheless brimming with emotion.<br /><br /><b>Mini synopsis</b><br />Waylander (lone-wolf, assassin and general kick-ass) saves a priest almost by accident which sets of a chain of world changing events. Waylander is set on an impossible mission and elsewhere, a major battle ensues. The story focuses on Waylander mostly but it does flick between his quest and the battle. <br /><br />This book is set before Legend (the first book published in the Drennai series), and Waylander’s actions are felt within Druss’s story. For anyone new to Gemmell I’d very much recommend reading Legend first as it’s one of the best (if not THE best) fantasy books ever. <br /><br />Format – ebook and audiobook<br />Pages – 384 (roughly 11 hours of audio plus some additional facts about how Gemmell came up with the idea which didn’t appear in the ebook)<br />Dumbass movie exec pitch – Think Legend, but with a crossbow and a legendary quest instead.<br /><br /><b>Writing</b><br />Gemmell’s writing is superior. In fact, I wish more authors would take note of Gemmell’s ability to cram such emotion, action and intrigue into so few words. In the hands of a lesser author, this book could easily have been 700-800 pages. <br /><br />His ability to clearly set up the conflict within the book, the mood of the characters and the dangers they face in very few sentences is impressive. <br /><br />Example:<br /><i>’Half the world would pay to spit on your grave.’</i><br />Gemmell skips the need to go over and over the deeds committed by Waylander in the past to (over)explain why people would find him despicable. Instead he uses fuelled sentences such as the above to paint a clear picture. <br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br /><b>Waylander</b> is the central character. A sort of anti-hero with an interesting past (all I can say without spoiling anything). He is a man who all have come to fear but a surprising, and mistaken, act of kindness changes the world forever (which is felt through future books in the series). <br /><br />The journey that Waylander goes through, not just physically, is fantastic to read and not only leaves you in awe of his brutal past and abilities, there are also moments of kindness that tug at the heart strings. <br /><br /><i>‘Death is being drawn to you from every side. You are trapped at the centre of a web of fate and the spiders are closing in.’</i><br /><br />Dardalion, the priest who Waylander meets at the start, also goes through an interesting story arc. There are other side characters that keep the story going too. Whilst these characters are not around for very long, Gemmell still manages to make them memorable. <br /><br />Also, his descriptions of characters help paint an instant picture:<br /><i>His mouth was lipless, his teeth like tombstones.</i><br /><br /><b>Themes</b><br />Does one heroic or great deed make up for a lifetime of sin? Is it too late to change your path and become a ‘goodguy’ even if you’ve made horrible decisions in your past? These are the recurring questions that run throughout this book and whilst simple, it is very powerful and is an interesting question to ponder. <br /><br />It’s also very thought-provoking on other levels. There are various interactions about spirituality and mortality. <br /><br /><b>Notable issues</b><br />Just one issue really and it had nothing to do with the story, which btw I wouldn’t change. The ebook version had multiple errors within it which threw me out of the story a couple of times. Other than that it was flawless, concise and awesome. <br /><br /><b>Final thought</b><br />I’m saddened that I never read any Gemmell books before he passed away and I can see why he is still a big influence to current fantasy writers. This book, and the other two in the series I’ve read so far, are perfect for reading in between big sagas. For instance, I’ve just finished Brandon Sanderson’s Oathbringer. Whilst that book was also five stars, it was a mammoth 1,244 pages. Waylander, at 384 pages packs a punch and is every bit as satisfying. <br /><br /><i>“When a fool sees himself as he is, then he is a fool no longer; and when a wise man learns of his own wisdom, then he becomes a fool.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18054538510732682770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_459099968" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459099968" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459099968?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459099968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5063045186294922813">This book drew me in like few books do. It <i>is</i> David Gemmell, so expect some familiar ground, such as ambiguous characters and gratuitous violence. It’s pulpy and atmospheric, two traits I often find endearing in (dark) fantasy fiction. The novel is really dark and brooding, just like the titular character, and there are some uncompromisingly grim scenes. Like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__Drenai_Saga___1_' title='Legend (Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Legend</a>, it’s a study of what it is that makes a man a “hero” (or an anti-hero, for that matter). We also get a glimpse into the conception</span>
  <span id="freeText5063045186294922813" style="display:none">This book drew me in like few books do. It <i>is</i> David Gemmell, so expect some familiar ground, such as ambiguous characters and gratuitous violence. It’s pulpy and atmospheric, two traits I often find endearing in (dark) fantasy fiction. The novel is really dark and brooding, just like the titular character, and there are some uncompromisingly grim scenes. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__Drenai_Saga___1_" title="Legend (Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a>, it’s a study of what it is that makes a man a “hero” (or an anti-hero, for that matter). We also get a glimpse into the conception and building of Dros Delnoch, the fortress that features so prominently in <i>Legend</i>, which I thought was neat. The novel has a surprisingly philosophical bent. The theme of redemption is present, as one would expect, although it manifests in unexpected forms. Other recurring themes are: prejudice, friendship, sacrifice and the meaning of faith. It’s all tied together.<br /><br />Gemmell also understood that sometimes less is more, and this is quite true here. The plot is actually kind of sparse, but it works well since the plot is arguably not the driving force behind this story. What is it that makes Waylander / Dakeyras tick? That is the question the book concerns itself with. The locations of the book were really great, ranging from besieged fortresses to windy steppes, giving the story an epic, sprawling feel, despite the fact that it isn’t a very long novel. As I have already mentioned, it is a violent story and there is plentiful action, all of it masterfully written.<br />And you just <i>have</i> to love the dialogue:	<br /><i>"Why are you always so unpleasant, Waylander?" <br />"Because I choose to be." <br />"In that case, I don't suppose you have many friends." <br />"I don't have any friends." </i><br /><br />I really enjoyed it. Perhaps in part due to timing (I read it on the back of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/88014.Karl_Edward_Wagner" title="Karl Edward Wagner" rel="nofollow noopener">Karl Edward Wagner</a>’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/715274.Dark_Crusade" title="Dark Crusade by Karl Edward Wagner" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Crusade</a>, and I was <i>really</i> just itching for some more dark, violent and fairly uncomplicated fantasy). Or… perhaps it was because of the <i>Shapeshifters</i>. But there it is. I think I’ll add this to my “favourites” shelf now. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5063045186294922813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_533980659" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/533980659?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer533980659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4548154167377141995">This is the first book in the series - chronologically; it is listed in publication order here. By this time we all know the big picture: the Drenai lands are overrun by an unstoppable force, the last groups of Drenai army continue desperate struggle against overwhelming odds, the simple farmers become reluctant heroes, etc. The main character of the book is an infamous assassin who managed to piss off almost everybody and is hunted by seemingly almost every single person in the world. A very in</span>
  <span id="freeText4548154167377141995" style="display:none">This is the first book in the series - chronologically; it is listed in publication order here. By this time we all know the big picture: the Drenai lands are overrun by an unstoppable force, the last groups of Drenai army continue desperate struggle against overwhelming odds, the simple farmers become reluctant heroes, etc. The main character of the book is an infamous assassin who managed to piss off almost everybody and is hunted by seemingly almost every single person in the world. A very insignificant event (he helped a tortured monk while recovering his stolen horse) set events in motion which gave him a chance to redeem himself by recovering a great relic for battered Drednai army. <br /><br />The main idea of the book is about redemption. I think it is slightly overplayed as a lot of bad people start doing good deeds without any visible motivation. In the end deux ex machina is used yet again cheapening otherwise very powerful last pages. The character of Waylander himself is interesting, but I really wish the book would start earlier when he was still an assassin for hire - we only see his evil deeds in his flashbacks. <br /><br />3.5 stars for a good book with some minor annoyances mentioned above which prevented me from rounding it up to 4. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4548154167377141995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3570963660" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3570963660" />
    <a title="Dawn C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14948447-dawn-c"><img alt="Dawn C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535435406p2/14948447.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3570963660?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn C" href="/user/show/14948447-dawn-c">Dawn C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3570963660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11408640582415560839"><i>”There is evil in all of us, and it is the mark of a man how he defies the evil within.”</i><br/><br/>This was an astoundingly good read! Waylander may be one of my all time favorite novels and deserves more than 5 stars. Gemmell’s writing is concise and beautiful, meaningful with a few words, not unlike the master Ursula Le Guin herself. I’m deeply affected by his characters, by these flawed people who do not wish to be heroes but find themselves moved by the people around them to do better despite themselve</span>
  <span id="freeText11408640582415560839" style="display:none"><i>”There is evil in all of us, and it is the mark of a man how he defies the evil within.”</i><br /><br />This was an astoundingly good read! Waylander may be one of my all time favorite novels and deserves more than 5 stars. Gemmell’s writing is concise and beautiful, meaningful with a few words, not unlike the master Ursula Le Guin herself. I’m deeply affected by his characters, by these flawed people who do not wish to be heroes but find themselves moved by the people around them to do better despite themselves. The themes revolve around redemption and trust and companionship. In a brutal, war torn world, there is softness between friends and lovers and it is freely expressed. Travel, introspection, honesty, conversation, those are the foundation on which Gemmell writes his stories and I’m here for it. I’m so glad I have stumbled upon his works which I’ve fallen head over heels in love with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11408640582415560839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1989997705?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1paper">1paper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1989997705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2075307146683645773">This is pre-<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___1_' title='Legend (The Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Legend</a> chronologically. We get to see how a couple of major items in Legend came to be & the forgotten sacrifices that fueled them. The main characters were rather complex & many weren't particularly nice, even if they were supposed to be good guys. It's not surprising that the main character was an antihero, but there is another heroic figure, a Drenai general, that is even better in many ways. Some of the supporting characters were far more sympathetic, pulled along by horrifying e</span>
  <span id="freeText2075307146683645773" style="display:none">This is pre-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___1_" title="Legend (The Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a> chronologically. We get to see how a couple of major items in Legend came to be &amp; the forgotten sacrifices that fueled them. The main characters were rather complex &amp; many weren't particularly nice, even if they were supposed to be good guys. It's not surprising that the main character was an antihero, but there is another heroic figure, a Drenai general, that is even better in many ways. Some of the supporting characters were far more sympathetic, pulled along by horrifying events just as the reader is. <br /><br />It's a very tough book to put down &amp; the end is an amazing crescendo of violent, nasty threads weaving together into a satisfying tapestry.<br /><br />I am not sure how I feel about the epilogue, though. It's a short chapter that sums up what happened afterward, sometimes years in the future. On the one hand, I loved it. It was satisfying on many levels. On the other hand, it could have made a book or two. Still, in keeping with Gemmell's terse style, it made more sense.<br /><br />I see at least one other reviewer compared it obliquely to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/88014.Karl_Edward_Wagner" title="Karl Edward Wagner" rel="nofollow noopener">Karl Edward Wagner</a>'s Kane books which are some of my favorites. It's a good comparison for the dark, gritty atmosphere. The main characters aren't of Kane's stature, but that makes it better in some ways - more realistic (for lack of a better term) &amp; gripping. I KNOW that Kane is going get through whatever horrible situation he's in, but that's not true of Gemmell's characters. He kills &amp; maims them often enough to keep me guessing.<br /><br />I think this book could be read first, so far. It wouldn't spoil anything &amp; might make 'Legend' even better.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2075307146683645773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_396025634" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396025634" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/396025634?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=age-adult">age-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=me-likey-mucho">me-likey-mucho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=sob-fest">sob-fest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=cut-my-heart-out">cut-my-heart-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad">why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=4-to-5-stars">4-to-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer396025634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16548379411277124968"><b>Final rating: 4.5/5 stars</b><br/><br/>I have read first two books in the series starting with publishing order, and i have to admit i was a bit confused at the world in this one because i didn't understand that it happens before <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___1_' title='Legend (The Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell' rel='nofollow noopener'> Legend</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/613991.The_King_Beyond_the_Gate__The_Drenai_Saga___2_' title='The King Beyond the Gate (The Drenai Saga, #2) by David Gemmell' rel='nofollow noopener'> The king beyond the gate</a> until i figured it out by certain hints. (I thought all books happen years and years in the future, but this book proved me wrong.)<br/><br/>Overall, this would be a first book in the series if started chronologically. But I wouldn't recommend starting out w</span>
  <span id="freeText16548379411277124968" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 4.5/5 stars</b><br><br>I have read first two books in the series starting with publishing order, and i have to admit i was a bit confused at the world in this one because i didn't understand that it happens before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___1_" title="Legend (The Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener"> Legend</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/613991.The_King_Beyond_the_Gate__The_Drenai_Saga___2_" title="The King Beyond the Gate (The Drenai Saga, #2) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener"> The king beyond the gate</a> until i figured it out by certain hints. (I thought all books happen years and years in the future, but this book proved me wrong.)<br><br>Overall, this would be a first book in the series if started chronologically. But I wouldn't recommend starting out with this one - better to start out with publishing order - it will be much easier to catch the hints and terms. <br><br>Anyway, this series is great because most of these books are stand alone - despite characters appearing sometimes in other books. What I also loved was the fact that this book was about how the organization of the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Thirty, which were a fraternity of warrior-monks, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> have been founded and for me, it was the greatest part of the story.<br><br>This book also features 3 particular main characters as a focus:<br>An antihero assassin, a priest who wanted to stop the killing of his brothers thus going against everything they believed in (that all life is precious), and a Drenai general. But there were also a lot more characters.<br><br>This story is not kind - Like in Legend, Gemmell didn't shy away from killing characters, even important ones. I barely contained my tears near the end.<br><br>Also, our wonderful cover:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449223540i/17253626.jpg" width="310" alt="look at that beautiful cover!!!!" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>STORY &amp; CHARACTERS</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>Orien, the famous King of the Drenai, abdicated in the favor of his kind and honorable son, Nialliad. But he didn't leave his legendary Bronze armor to his heir. Many years later, Vagrian forces started invading Drenai, and to make things worse, Drenai King Nialliad was murdered by an assassin with a crossbow. Things are getting worse day by day, the fortress/port city of Dros Purdol is under siege and some forces are hidden in the Skultik Forest. But one of the worst things is hunting down, torturing and murdering priests of the Source - who have strong magical abilities, even capable of killing people. But they took a wow to never harm anyone and this is why they die, never able to defend themselves, else they betray everything they fought for. Their arch enemies are Dark Brotherhood, who use their powers to hurt people in spirit realm and in the human realm.<br><br>One of the priests of the Source, Dardalion, is captured and tortured for fun, until one man interupts them and demands his stolen horse back. That man is the assassin called Waylander, who has a really notorious reputation. Waylander didn't want to free Dardalion at first, but changed his mind. And after they started traveling together, they met Danyal and her children. Once again, Waylander thinks his decisions over and in the end accepts to help her and her children in order to lead them to safety. <br><br>But during the way, Dardalion is attacked by a group of Dark Brotherhood in the spirit realm, and to help him (to wake him up) Waylander was forced to feed him his blood, which in turn turns Dardalion into someone else - a man who was a pacifist and wouldn't hurt anyone now wants to fight back and even kill people like the members of Dark Brotherhood.<br><br>During one of the nights, a blind man appears in front of the group and says to Waylander that there is a way for his redemption. Once upon a time, the old man was called Orien, and the only thing that can help save Drenai, raise the moral of the soldiers, is his legendary "magic" armor of Bronze which should be delivered to general Egel. After all, Waylander is the assassin who murdered Orien's son for money. <br><br>Now hunted by Dark Brotherhood, Nadir forces, Vagrian's forces and their general Kaem, and also by a famed assassin, Cadoras the Stalker, Waylander must go into enemy territory, to Raboas, where the Bronze Armor is hiden. <br><br>In the fort where the attack is happening, Drenai officer Gellan and his other comrades struggle with the Vagrian forces and they must hold out until Drenai general Karnak arrive with the reinforcements, so they could go into Dros Purdol, get into the city to break the siege. <br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>CHARACTERS</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>Waylander</b> is a famous assassin who had changed after the death of his family. When his family was murdered he set on a revenge spree and murdered the killers, and later started career as an assassin. But his latest murder, murder of his own King for money, was the point of no return. Betrayed by his employer, Kaem, he tries to escape but also kills Kaem's own son, thus making an enemy of both nations. Once ruthless, jaded man, he saves a priest of the Source, Dardalion, by whim and discovers that the priest himself had much more impact on his personality than ever. Now his only chance to redeem himself for everything comes in the quest for Bronze Armour. <br><br>{I myself can't tell how I feel about him, despite him being anti hero - which I like to read about as they are so rare - he just didn't work out for me in the way for me to like or hate him. He was solid and okay character all in all.}<br><br><b>Dardalion</b> is a priest who was saved by a whim from being tortured to death. He is a mystic and thus is able to see emotions and memories from the clothes, which usually horrifies him as he sees many unpleasant things, he can expel his soul and scout the ground, and do many other things. But his order doesn't allow murder - their power is too great to be used like their enemies, Dark Brotherhood, do. But, after being tainted by blood of Waylander, his opinions changed - he is still true to the source but someone must take a fall and start battling against Dark Brotherhood. The way it was going, the Source Priests would all die suffering, and there wouldn't be anyone to stop them. Thus he becomes the first Battle Priest of the Source. <br><br>{Dardalion made me smile, he is so honest and kind, and even knowing so many things, he wages a battle of his own - to serve the source by keeping it's priests alive, no matter what the cost. Overall, I enjoyed every single moment with him, he was just wonderful.}<br><br><b>Danyal, her daughters and son</b> are refugees, who struggle to stay alive. Danyal, a former actress, would do anything to survive, even accepting help from the murderer. But Danyal is judgmental, hurt by so many people she finds it hard to trust again as before. <br><br>{Danyal's big problem is her judgmental nature - and she won't listen to reasons. In any case, she is the character i liked the least in this whole book. She is a fighter and she won't give up, but her personality is different matter.}<br><br><b>Durmast</b> is Waylander's "friend" in the same career as he.<br><br><b>Cadoras</b> is an assassin who is hired to kill Waylander, but he wants to do it properly.<br><br><b>Kaem</b> is the Vagrian general who hired Waylander to murder Drenai's King, but in the process betrayed Waylander, who, by accident, killed his son during his escape. Now he won't stop at nothing until he gets the fortress under siege, the Bronze Armor and Waylander's head.<br><br><b>Karnak</b> is a famous Drenai general who wants to save the fortress and also get a bigger reputation. Overall, he is capable and charismatic leader who boosts the moral of the people. <br><br><b>Gellan, Jonat and Sarvaj </b> are Drenai officers who are currently under the attack in the fort. Gellan is a former friend of Waylander, he knew Waylander 20 years ago when hey had been best friends. But tragedy found him too, but he chose to stay a soldier and fight till the end. Jonat is the man who despises all nobles and Sarvaj is honorable man who disapporoves the fact Gellan strives to make Jonat into a leader - knowing that Jonat has absolutely no respect for Gellan and that he hates every single noble that exists.<br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>OVERALL</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>Interesting book, not as strong as Legend was - but I still loved it. Overall, would I recommend someone to read chronologically? The answer is no. Do not start with this book. The system of magic is a bit more explained in the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___1_" title="Legend (The Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener"> Legend</a>, and it would be easier if you know some things in advance. This will be a welcome surprise then. <br><br>I will sum up what I generally think about it this way:<br><br><i>
  <b>LIKED: </b>
</i><br>☑ Drenai history + how certain organizations came to be.<br>☑ Dardalion is probably the best character in this book. I also loved Gellan and Sarvaj and some other side characters too. I was surprised by the actions of certain people and this is also a +.<br>☑ The Magic System.<br>☑ The emotion level warning.<br>☑ Story.<br>☑ Realistic portrayal of war.<br>☑ Paranormal creatures.<br>☑ Return of familiar terms like Armour of Bronze, Nadir, Drenai people, Source... etc.<br><br><i>
  <b>SO-SO: </b>
</i><br>☐ Waylander is an interesting character, but I dont feel anything about him.<br>☐ Karnak was interesting and he plays one of the important parts in the story, but I dont like him, nor I hate him. The same goes for Durmast &amp; Cadoras as well.<br><br><i>
  <b>DISLIKED: </b>
</i><br>☒ Insta-love/hate: From bitter enemies to "I love you." It makes it kind of unbelievable. <br>☒ Main female character Danyal. She was just plain boring and very, very irritating. Thankfully, only 15% or so include her POVs. <br>☒ Like I said above, lack of strong female leads. Danyal basically leaves <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her children <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> to search for adventure. That doesn't sound like resposible <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[mother <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br>☒ Wishing there was more about Egel, since he plays one of the important parts in the book. <br>☒ Fast pacing. I mean too fast.<br><br><b>
  <i>OTHER IMPORTANT INFO:</i>
</b><br>⚠ <b>Standalone:</b> YES.<br>⚠ <b>Point of View:</b> Third POV, multiply characters.<br>⚠ <b>Cliffhanger:</b> Nonexistent. <br>⚠ <b>Triggers:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rape, torture, they are at war, lots of character deaths...  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>⚠ <b>Love triangle:</b> No.<br>⚠ <b>Angst:</b> There is. <br>⚠ <b>Supernatural:</b> Yes. Group of specific magicians who can expel their souls, command the bodies of other people etc. Some other creatures are in it too. <br>⚠ <b>Explicit content:</b> Mentioned.<br>⚠ <b>Ending type:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ HEA, the best that could be salvaged <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>⚠ <b>Note:</b> Do not read this series in chronological order. Trust me.<br>____________________________________________<br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br>____________________________________________ <br><br><b>REVIEW(S) RELATED TO THIS BOOK:</b><br><br>◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396025606" rel="nofollow noopener"> Legend (Drenai Saga, #1) </a> <br>◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396025634" rel="nofollow noopener"> Waylander (Drenai Saga, #3) </a> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

Each seems to benefit from the influence of the other as Waylander saves a women and her young charges, rediscovering his humanity along the way whereas Dardalion decides to take up the battle. Together, they help thwart the plans of Kaem to permanently rid the lands of the Drenai forever. Waylander then embarks on a hopeless mission to retrieve a symbolic set of bronze armor to help rally the Drenai. The book does not shy away from depicting the horrors of war and man at his worst (and best.) </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1052711704?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Ionson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Ionson" href="/user/show/20993440-daniel-ionson">Daniel Ionson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20993440-daniel-ionson?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20993440-daniel-ionson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20993440-daniel-ionson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1052711704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1475393027593576781">It’s safe to say that Gemmell was a major mover (hard to say if he was “The” mover) in the new paradigm within the Fantasy genre towards a level of realism and grit which has now become so popular over the past 15 years. But my feeling is that those trying to imitate his style often fail by going over-the-top. Gemmell’s powerful effect comes with his realism, not with gratuitous violence, etc.. <br/><br/>The strength of this book is in the believable, complex depth of the protagonist. Waylander was pushed</span>
  <span id="freeText1475393027593576781" style="display:none">It’s safe to say that Gemmell was a major mover (hard to say if he was “The” mover) in the new paradigm within the Fantasy genre towards a level of realism and grit which has now become so popular over the past 15 years. But my feeling is that those trying to imitate his style often fail by going over-the-top. Gemmell’s powerful effect comes with his realism, not with gratuitous violence, etc.. <br /><br />The strength of this book is in the believable, complex depth of the protagonist. Waylander was pushed (as so many people) into darkness by the cruelty of the world, by profound love that is ripped away from us, leaving us wounded to the core. As so often happens, these wounds get infected, and we stray into evil. <br /><br />But in spite of all of the darkness that he delves into, his soul keep yearning for life and light again. That struggle is what makes this worth reading. That humanness is what truly puts Gemmell on the map. I can’t recommend this one highly enough. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1475393027593576781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_245222398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/245222398" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/245222398?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Ryan" href="/user/show/7151669-anthony-ryan">Anthony Ryan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer245222398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18347840829294370896">Redemption was always one of David Gemmell's most persistent themes, perhaps finding its most compelling expression in this tale of Dakeyras the Waylander, an apparently heartless assassin caught up in a brutal invasion of the Drenai homeland. Gemmell's depiction of war eschews any comfortable fantasy conventions to present something every bit as ugly as real-world conflict, complete with massacre and rape. However, it's the characterisation that really shines here; by being compelled to reconne</span>
  <span id="freeText18347840829294370896" style="display:none">Redemption was always one of David Gemmell's most persistent themes, perhaps finding its most compelling expression in this tale of Dakeyras the Waylander, an apparently heartless assassin caught up in a brutal invasion of the Drenai homeland. Gemmell's depiction of war eschews any comfortable fantasy conventions to present something every bit as ugly as real-world conflict, complete with massacre and rape. However, it's the characterisation that really shines here; by being compelled to reconnect with humanity Dakeyras rediscovers his soul. The character proved enough of a draw to spawn two sequels which are well worth reading, but don't quite reach the same heights. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18347840829294370896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2287575458" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2287575458" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66331236-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568827728p2/66331236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2287575458?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/66331236-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19041006-waylander">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66331236-lyn?shelf=waylander">waylander</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2287575458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7925343159942768042">This is the first book introducing the dark and deadly assassin, Waylander. I liked him from the start. I guess mostly because I have a soft spot for tortured anti-heroes. Waylander wasn’t a hero, no. In fact, he’s the living embodiment of the saying “No Good Deed Goes Unpunished.”<br/><br/>Waylander was once a man named Dakeyras. His life took a dark turn and could have spiraled on like that. Then he went and did a good deed which ended up haunting him and forced him to reassess his life. His life is tra</span>
  <span id="freeText7925343159942768042" style="display:none">This is the first book introducing the dark and deadly assassin, Waylander. I liked him from the start. I guess mostly because I have a soft spot for tortured anti-heroes. Waylander wasn’t a hero, no. In fact, he’s the living embodiment of the saying “No Good Deed Goes Unpunished.”<br /><br />Waylander was once a man named Dakeyras. His life took a dark turn and could have spiraled on like that. Then he went and did a good deed which ended up haunting him and forced him to reassess his life. His life is tragic yes, but the man he became, the assassin, Waylander the Slayer, was a force of nature.<br /><br />His sense of survival, his self-awareness of danger was incredible. His fighting skills were spooky, legendary. I loved his interactions with Danyal and the children. Danyal suited him to a T. She was the perfect fit for him, strong in spite of everything she went through.<br /><br />David Gemmell crafted a complicated, interesting plot-line that kept me turning the page. Waylander was my favorite character and writing this review makes me want to read his story again.<br /><br /><a href="https://nomadicworlds.wordpress.com/2018/03/02/book-review-waylander-david-gemmell/" rel="nofollow noopener">Posted on Blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7925343159942768042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kitvaria by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/22778865-g-r-matthews">G.R. Matthews</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1126371-kitvaria-sarene?shelf=fantasy-all-subgenres">fantasy-all-subgenres</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1897387882" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16780715236697644919">Finally I managed to get around to reading my very first Gemmell! It will definitely not be my last one...<br/>I really enjoyed the story - especially the characters. Waylander is a great character to follow - I had a thing for him from the moment when a priest asked him to save him from death, and Waylander answers "Why?" Just my kind of character to follow around! I liked the others too, and was glad to be able to spend so much time with them.<br/>The plot was interesting, and for me had a good balance </span>
  <span id="freeText16780715236697644919" style="display:none">Finally I managed to get around to reading my very first Gemmell! It will definitely not be my last one...<br />I really enjoyed the story - especially the characters. Waylander is a great character to follow - I had a thing for him from the moment when a priest asked him to save him from death, and Waylander answers "Why?" Just my kind of character to follow around! I liked the others too, and was glad to be able to spend so much time with them.<br />The plot was interesting, and for me had a good balance between a bit of politic, lots of action, quite some quests and adventures, a siege and being thrown into the army life quite a bit.<br /><br />I give only 4 stars because of A) the characters changing a bit too much way to fast for my personal liking, some solutions being just a bit TOO easy and parts of it being quite predictable. Since it was out way before most of the other fantasy books, it isn't at fault for being predictable - most classics are in a way - as so many others have taken their inspirations from the older titles.<br /><br />I did like just how dark it was for a classic - it felt a bit like the start of nowadays grimdark books to me - and I once again liked the balance Gemmell strikes between despair and hope, blood and beauty, fight and faith, grit and adventure.<br /><br />My ebook copy had quite some little typos, I would not expect that from a professionally published ebook, but the prose was fluent and good enough to let me flow by tose and ignore them without getting annoyed.<br /><br />If you haven't yet tried Gemmell - I definitely recommend it! One of the only classics besides LOTR that really could hook me completely!</span>

<div id="review_3159682971" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3159682971" />
    <a title="Alfred Haplo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34550725-alfred-haplo"><img alt="Alfred Haplo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599680519p2/34550725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3159682971?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alfred Haplo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alfred Haplo" href="/user/show/34550725-alfred-haplo">Alfred Haplo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=sf-fantasy-mytho">sf-fantasy-mytho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=1970-to-1999">1970-to-1999</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3159682971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7475071704825583392">To be remembered as just one of many in a series. <i>Waylander</i> * precedes <i>Legend</i> by scores of years, with references to the origins of Del Denoch, The Thirty and the Armour of Bronze. For these fan-pleasing references and the events in <i>Waylander</i> that precipitated these series landmarks, an extra half star for the rating. <br/><br/>Stylistically, it was similar to my previous three Gemmells ** (so far), as were the types of characters. By that, expect artificial, contrived dialogue and sentimental awkwardness</span>
  <span id="freeText7475071704825583392" style="display:none">To be remembered as just one of many in a series. <i>Waylander</i> * precedes <i>Legend</i> by scores of years, with references to the origins of Del Denoch, The Thirty and the Armour of Bronze. For these fan-pleasing references and the events in <i>Waylander</i> that precipitated these series landmarks, an extra half star for the rating. <br /><br />Stylistically, it was similar to my previous three Gemmells ** (so far), as were the types of characters. By that, expect artificial, contrived dialogue and sentimental awkwardness from two-dimensional fatalistic characters, but they were effective enough for plots that were summaries rather than fully-fleshed out. Despite logistical challenges, the tide could be turned in one fell swoop. Yet, I appreciated Gemmell’s economy of words for large-scale action without going overboard with the emoting and the philosophizing. Throw in some cynical humor, the feisty-lady-lover, the warrior-monk and bloodshed, and a new Drenai book was in the making. Gemmell, if nothing else, had larger-than-life heroism defined to a science.<br /><br /><i>Waylander</i> had all that, but missing the big gut-punching moments for me. The kind that would spring tears to my eyes because, Valor. Courage. Sacrifice. There was a bit of that towards the end, but the protagonist - Waylander - himself was on a separate redemptive quest over and above the carnage at the fort. Yes, he killed enemies in the thick of it along with everyone else armed with a weapon and a prayer, as his journey intersected with the ongoing wars between the Nadir and the Drenai, which form the backbone of the series (so far). Yet, he was distant, removed from the reader's engagement. Perhaps mine was just focused on the sieges, on the would-be heroes in Karnak, Dardalion, Gellan and other books' protagonists who fought to die for a cause, for their people, in the here and now. There was a grander quest and a moral sacrifice greater than the individual. Here, Waylander was also on a mission to die, but his personal quest to retrieve the armor seemed small in comparison. He was not saving others, he was saving himself. I was not moved by it. <br /><br />It didn’t help knowing upfront that our eponymous hero lived past this book into the trilogy. That took away some suspense in an environment where no one was generally safe in a Gemmell story. As an avenger turned deadly assassin feared by all, the Slayer didn’t live up to his reputation. Within the first chapters, he saved victims from rape and torture, wept for his dead family, loved, cradled children, and protected the innocent. For most of the story, he was unfailingly compassionate (but gruffly so because, strong man), and unfailingly gentle (but rebuffed reciprocity because, death to those who loved him). For a supposedly complex character, he was a rather uncomplicated person. I don't read Gemmell to feed my inner human being, I read him to feed the chest-thumping, lion-roaring, ambivalent pretentious hero. The best parts of this story belonged to the morally ambiguous and the morally conflicted. Neither described the Waylander. <br /><br /><br />[* <i>Legend</i> (#1 Drenai), <i>The King Beyond the Gate</i> (#2 Drenai), <i>Knights of Dark Renown</i><br />** Waylander sub-series: <i>Waylander</i> (#3 Drenai, #1 Waylander)<i>In the Realm of the Wolf</i> (#5 Drenai, #2 Waylander), <i>Hero in the Shadows</i> (#9 Drenai, #3 Waylander)]</span>
  <a data-text-id="7475071704825583392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_371618671" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/371618671" />
    <a title="D.E.M. Emrys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11073300-d-e-m-emrys"><img alt="D.E.M. Emrys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350307468p2/11073300.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/371618671?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="D.E.M. Emrys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="D.E.M. Emrys" href="/user/show/11073300-d-e-m-emrys">D.E.M. Emrys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer371618671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3694947667251456839"><i> Can you put a price on redemption?<br/><br/> The King is dead, and thousands are set to follow him. Drenai land is swept into the tides of war. Enemy soldiers sweep across the country, butchering man, woman and babe. It is a dark time, and dark work is at play.<br/><br/> Can salvation be earned?<br/><br/> Dardalion is a man of the light, a dying light in the dark days. But, he must confront the evil, and to face it a man must walk the shadows.<br/><br/> Karnak is a hero, a beacon of hope in the night. He kindles fire in the hearts of</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3694947667251456839" style="display:none"><i> Can you put a price on redemption?<br /><br /> The King is dead, and thousands are set to follow him. Drenai land is swept into the tides of war. Enemy soldiers sweep across the country, butchering man, woman and babe. It is a dark time, and dark work is at play.<br /><br /> Can salvation be earned?<br /><br /> Dardalion is a man of the light, a dying light in the dark days. But, he must confront the evil, and to face it a man must walk the shadows.<br /><br /> Karnak is a hero, a beacon of hope in the night. He kindles fire in the hearts of men, but his ambition burns brighter than the sun – and there is only room for one sun in the sky.<br /><br /> Waylander is a dark man; a hunter and a killer. Neither light nor torch can burn bright beside him, but no shadow is too dark for him to walk.<br /><br /> War can be won by strength, bravery and the hearts of good men. Yet, there is a path of shadows where neither hero nor torch can stray. But only dark men can walk the shadows. There is only one man for the job. But can he be trusted to save the Drenai?<br /><br /> For he is an assassin – a traitor – the man who killed the king.<br /><br /> He is Waylander.</i><br /><br /><br /> Waylander is the third novel that David Gemmell wrote in the Drenai series. Set before his debut ‘Legend’, Waylander provides a legacy to Gemmell’s later works. As with other works by the author, the theme of redemption runs strong throughout, and though good and evil are at odds, the shades of grey divide the battlefields.<br /><br /> The main drive, as with all of Gemmell’s novels, is the characterisation. From the Priest Dardalion who battles with his will to do good, to the General and war-hero Karnak, each and every soul in this book is well fleshed. That’s actually a good way of putting it. Soul. That’s what each of Gemmell’s characters embodies. They aren’t just fictional marionettes toyed with for the readers’ pleasure. They live, they breathe, they fight, love and laugh. They have soul. And, that is why I love Gemmell.<br /><br /> ...and that’s without even tackling the title character! Waylander is the anti-hero to Gemmell’s Druss the Legend. But, Waylander’s tragedy and choices, in my eyes, make him a richer character in some respects. He doesn’t just earn his place in reader’s hearts, he fights for it.<br /><br /> Gemmell has always written with a sharpened quill, crisp and quick. The story is fast paced and action packed, keeping the reader hooked throughout. There’s little room to catch a breath, and the first time I read Waylander, there was little room for me to sleep seeing as I finished it in a single night.<br /><br /> As stated earlier, Waylander is set years before Legend. But, the novel sets up a legacy for the later book in the series, namely the warrior priest sect The Thirty, and Karnak. These extra touches, weaves and webs to a fully envisioned world, add an epic scale to the Drenai saga, creating a fully realised world that, though fictional, feels lived in.<br /><br /> There are small evils and small goods to all men. But men are still men, they do wrong and they do right. Gemmell was an author that explored the limited strengths of the human being, and showed us what it was like to be a man. He sets the standard for idols, role models, and heroes.<br /><br /> After reading Waylander...you’ll want to be a man.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3694947667251456839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_450108906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450108906" />
    <a title="Anders" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14054706-anders"><img alt="Anders" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420457294p2/14054706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/450108906?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anders" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anders" href="/user/show/14054706-anders">Anders</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14054706-anders?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14054706-anders?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer450108906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6728450709177253007">“My enemies can soar into the night like invisible demons, conjure wolf creatures from hell, and read minds. On our side is a god that can lead a man to a ferry!” <br/><br/>Waylander is chronologically the first novel in the Drenai series. It starts with the king having been assassinated, and ruthless enemy troops swarming into Drenai lands, massacring the natives. This could mean the end for the Drenai. <br/><br/>Waylander walks these lands, a stone-hearted warrior, the assassin that killed the king. He is a man p</span>
  <span id="freeText6728450709177253007" style="display:none">“My enemies can soar into the night like invisible demons, conjure wolf creatures from hell, and read minds. On our side is a god that can lead a man to a ferry!” <br /><br />Waylander is chronologically the first novel in the Drenai series. It starts with the king having been assassinated, and ruthless enemy troops swarming into Drenai lands, massacring the natives. This could mean the end for the Drenai. <br /><br />Waylander walks these lands, a stone-hearted warrior, the assassin that killed the king. He is a man pursued, by his own demons, and a vast range of enemies. When his horse is stolen in the night, he pursues the men, and kills them all, by chance rescuing the pacifist priest Dardalion. This encounter changes the lives of both men. As their people are dying around them, they find they have to confront their beliefs and what they fight for. <br /><br />Meanwhile the scattered Drenai forces are surrounded everywhere they go. We follow the loyal and hard working officer Gellan, and the brilliant but overly ambitious general Karnak. Against overwhelming odds they must fight a battle to save the Drenai from the invading forces. <br /><br />The characterization is what drives the book forward. Each character is fleshed out, so you see their lust, their greed, their love, their hate, their compassion. Far too many novels like this you find it hard to believe what you are reading, but never with Gemmell, who put his heart and soul into every page. <br /><br />"There is evil in all of us, and it is the mark of a man how he defies the evil within.” <br /><br />It has a fair amount of resemblance to other Drenai books I have read, but it is conveyed in such a way here, that it only serves to strengthen the overall story and plot.<br /><br />Highly recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6728450709177253007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
