<div id="review_801234387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/801234387" />
    <a title="Laura Hughes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23686292-laura-hughes"><img alt="Laura Hughes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499452171p2/23686292.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801234387?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Hughes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Hughes" href="/user/show/23686292-laura-hughes">Laura Hughes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356501390" href="/book/show/13706717-waylander">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801234387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18218726721616146165">This is my first outing with David Gemmell, and I have to say I’m ashamed I waited this long to read his work. Gemmell is one of the legendary forerunners of modern fantasy, and has influenced many of my favourite authors, particularly those who write gritty ‘grimdark’ fantasy such as Joe Abercrombie. I expected big things from David Gemmell, and for the most part Waylander delivered them.<br/><br/>My first impression of Waylander was that there wasn’t much detail. Gemmell wasn’t telling me much about the</span>
  <span id="freeText18218726721616146165" style="display:none">This is my first outing with David Gemmell, and I have to say I’m ashamed I waited this long to read his work. Gemmell is one of the legendary forerunners of modern fantasy, and has influenced many of my favourite authors, particularly those who write gritty ‘grimdark’ fantasy such as Joe Abercrombie. I expected big things from David Gemmell, and for the most part Waylander delivered them.<br /><br />My first impression of Waylander was that there wasn’t much detail. Gemmell wasn’t telling me much about the characters – how they were feeling, what they’d been doing, why they were there – and I felt somewhat disconnected from them, particularly as we’re thrown into the action without being introduced to any of the characters involved. However, about 50 pages into the novel I realised how clever this was: we don’t necessarily need to know everything about the characters in order to empathise with them. It’s very much a case of judging characters by their actions during the current and ongoing events. Gemmell shows us how his characters act, providing limited or no information about their background; it’s up to the reader to witness their actions and decide for themselves how they feel about each character. <br /><br />This makes it particularly interesting, since there are characters whose reputation or situation would make them appear to be villains, yet whose actions define them otherwise, and vice versa. The characters are not blank slates, created by the author to be gradually filled in for us through the course of the story; rather, we get the feeling that they exist independently of the reader, and we just happen to catch glimpses of them at certain points in their lives. We are unaware of each character’s ‘normal’ behaviour: we simply see them as they are, and this makes our connection with them feel natural and unforced, our own choice rather than the author’s manipulation. <br /><br />Events in the novel are presented in a similar way. Gemmell shows rather than tells, and has a way of writing that is fairly minimal. His narrative is somewhat brisk in tone, and yet the action is vivid and the characters are well-drawn. His understated yet captivating style is surprisingly hard-hitting, and his ability to create moments of emotion and tragedy in just a page or two is astounding. An example of this is the tale of the old general Gan Degas. We only meet this character once – his entire character arc spans about four or five pages at the most – yet his sad story completely choked me up (and stuck in my memory so much that I remembered his name without having to look it up).<br /><br />The book isn’t perfect. I felt that Waylander’s shift from ‘Slayer’ to ‘hero’ would have been a lot more effective if it hadn’t happened right at the beginning (literally during the first couple of pages). We aren’t really shown much of him as the ruthless Slayer; as such I felt that his inner conflict – the pitiless man he was vs. the compassionate man he now is – isn’t quite as powerful as it could be. I also felt that some of the events – particularly the various battles – felt a bit disconnected from the rest of the story, and that the side-plot with the armour (and its importance in the grand scheme of things) was a little bit tenuous and contrived. However, there are many, many books in the overall series aside from this one, and it’s highly likely that I’m not seeing the full picture yet; and despite these minor complaints, I really was blown away by this writer. <br /><br />Although I am ashamed not to have read his work sooner, I’m excited to know that it’s all laid out before me now, waiting to be read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18218726721616146165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_678991293" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/678991293" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9839433-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604013299p2/9839433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/678991293?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/9839433-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356501390" href="/book/show/13706717-waylander">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9839433-grace?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer678991293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5206686479444371748">2.5/5 stars. It's a shame, but what I'm starting to suspect from David Gemmell novels is that if you've read one of his, you've read them all.<br/>I mean you have the old weathered soldier who has lived a morally suspect life, has contemplated retirement, has the same realist "shit happens, but oh well" philosophy usually as a result of a violent, bloody past, with many regrets (and usually his wife and kids have been slaughtered in some kind of awful fashion) - But due to strange circumstance or "fa</span>
  <span id="freeText5206686479444371748" style="display:none">2.5/5 stars. It's a shame, but what I'm starting to suspect from David Gemmell novels is that if you've read one of his, you've read them all.<br />I mean you have the old weathered soldier who has lived a morally suspect life, has contemplated retirement, has the same realist "shit happens, but oh well" philosophy usually as a result of a violent, bloody past, with many regrets (and usually his wife and kids have been slaughtered in some kind of awful fashion) - But due to strange circumstance or "fate" he decides to clean up his act and fight one last time, on a seemingly impossible quest to do this "one good deed" and either die or not in a blaze of glory. I mean this story alone sounds pretty promising, pretty awesome, but after three carbon copies of the same story and cardboard cut-outs for characters... It... Gets samey. <br /><br />There were a few very annoying things, that paired with how similar it is with his preceeding novels that caused me to knock this off a star. *Warning Rant Ahead*<br /><br />I didn't get this so much in "Legend" but in this book and "King Beyond the Gate" the women are all so thoroughly two dimensional, so throwaway and pathetic, and are all treated as such. I'm pretty sure every female character in this book (other than the two children) were painted as "whores" or rape victims, both of which are shown as irritating nags when they don't bend to the MC's will at the flick of a wrist (don't worry, they usually do). Danyal, for example, multiple rape victim, get's talked to like absolute shit by Waylander, Waylander says "he would never go with a woman he wouldn't pay for", this is the basic extent of their conversation before she falls head over heels in love with him. Sounds legit. He also physically abuses a prostitute, leaving bruises on her arm saying he got "carried away" - this is especially problematic because he's frequently described that despite his many flaws, he would never abuse a woman, by the narrater! Clearly you do tho. Rape tropes in fantasy are cliche, but when they're used as a plot device and gratuitously, it's cheap, and grating, not to mention disrespectful.<br /><br />/rant.<br /><br />Despite all this I wouldn't say this was an *awful* book, and I can definitely see why people would be happy to get away from the stodgey descriptions and intimidating tomes that usually permeate the fantasy genre. These books are fun, uncomplicated, and the action scenes are fantastic. Unfortunately I would suggest that unless you're happy with the same story being fed over and over again to purchase Legend and not bother with the two suceeding novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5206686479444371748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2768348906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2768348906" />
    <a title="Dan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5411470-dan"><img alt="Dan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587053101p2/5411470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2768348906?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan" href="/user/show/5411470-dan">Dan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5411470-dan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2768348906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6207101288074447238">I listened to this in audio book form. It has a linear plot without too many characters or complications, perfect for the format!<br/><br/>The book starts out in very exciting fashion: an evil assassin annoys himself by saving a priest about to be slaughtered who was in turn trying ineffectually to protect a young woman and her child. The rest of the novel's premise is essentially trying to figure out why the assassin would want at this late date in his life to redeem himself. In fact it's the assassin's </span>
  <span id="freeText6207101288074447238" style="display:none">I listened to this in audio book form. It has a linear plot without too many characters or complications, perfect for the format!<br /><br />The book starts out in very exciting fashion: an evil assassin annoys himself by saving a priest about to be slaughtered who was in turn trying ineffectually to protect a young woman and her child. The rest of the novel's premise is essentially trying to figure out why the assassin would want at this late date in his life to redeem himself. In fact it's the assassin's journey of self-exploration that makes the story so compelling. Thrown in as a bonus, we also have to try to figure out why the Source priest would reject his formerly pacifist stance and become militant. The love story is also wonderful.<br /><br />If the novel had stayed on this theme and kept centered on these three characters, it would have garnered five stars from me. Unfortunately, other characters come in and we get battles between two peoples, a hopeless quest undertaken for reasons never quite illuminated, a storming of the castle, a holding of this fortress. After a while, the book began to read like a history book. Only it's fake history. True yet remote history is only moderately interesting. Why would anyone care about a made-up history?<br /><br />For its meanderings I have to subtract one full star. The great part of the story is certain of the central characters, coupled with Gemmell's deep pronouncements on morality and the human condition. Omit the pointless history lesson, and I could ask for no more from a story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6207101288074447238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12339738122633408488">My second outing into the Drenai novels, the first being Legend. <br/><br/>(mild spoiler)<br/><br/><br/><br/>This book isn't without faults, one thing that struck me as lazy was how the main character is saved from an imminent death on two occasions by having earlier spared enemies he would have otherwise killed. Once was good, but using the same formula a second time fairly soon after the first lessened the impact somewhat. Though I should say that the second saviour soon became a favourite of mine. <br/><br/>BUT!!!!!<br/><br/>That and the oth</span>
  <span id="freeText12339738122633408488" style="display:none">My second outing into the Drenai novels, the first being Legend. <br /><br />(mild spoiler)<br /><br /><br /><br />This book isn't without faults, one thing that struck me as lazy was how the main character is saved from an imminent death on two occasions by having earlier spared enemies he would have otherwise killed. Once was good, but using the same formula a second time fairly soon after the first lessened the impact somewhat. Though I should say that the second saviour soon became a favourite of mine. <br /><br />BUT!!!!!<br /><br />That and the other niggles are utterly without significance when set against how GOOD the story is. The pace is blistering and the characters interesting (perhaps a few come across as samey but when we're dealing with elite killers you tend to need another elite killer to deal with them) and Gemmell's trademark take on war and the men that wage them. <br /><br />In all honesty I devoured this book in 2 sittings with a tiny 3rd when I thought I had some time but life beckoned. <br /><br />I look forward to more from the master of heroic fantasy. <br /><br />"No one pays for lambs."</span>

<div id="review_1055264841" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1055264841" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2346680-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357620152p2/2346680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1055264841?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/2346680-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780307797506" href="/book/show/11464110-waylander">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1055264841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9379154475706709208">Unlike <a href='http://ift.tt/1nl9iV8' rel='nofollow noopener'>my ambivalence to Tenaka Khan</a>, I very much liked the eponymous Waylander (aka Dakeyras) as an imperfect hero (he's not quite the anti-hero, though he skirts that line nicely). Also, I enjoy the fact that I get to use "eponymous" in a review; happens far too rarely.<br/><br/>When I first started <u>Waylander (Drenai Saga, #3)</u>, it took me a while before I realized that I was reading a prequel to the two books (<a href='http://email.ifttt.com/wf/click?upn=jGHDfwvrKDxaofcg5GVulg9CQ9akl7TWey9wviWZQJM-3D_bM0v-2Fecqq1kET4-2B3AH3g8cUy7KuK0lvX75Kf8LifO-2BBpV0eHEe-2BfWsH-2BqLuRjd1udgb1fJSnj1Y4LFAfCBFds-2FpTiJBSL-2FrLqfRLjSZXlqb8yW1qCCrzqb-2Fgnv2fXBpc88jvcEzZsGgwhQxQ-2FdvpJjomFs6-2BifL0gdNnkTBE8vCIMTnXSllI3SLqR4y6NGRvGleoEVwxbFEVtQ6GgYXnpHgzZ9hZfXC215LWsqdZHlrY4DBy0ECyA0N0eJUv7wzRPr6R0TMh-2FAOabTbyN6S6kBk9f7QSn4df2ITEQUjRls4Ts-2FSZ7heCzYI6TZGh0IG3GYqg9dHgErFKesjOxkAY5ho7dK4Ef5uyUuSueACa34FQxsk6rueC7xMr3sW9-2BoYh0XXDpwVeF-2F2S9vuiZcp0bg-3D-3D' rel='nofollow noopener'>#1</a>, <a href='http://ift.tt/1nl9iV8' rel='nofollow noopener'>#2</a>) that had come before. It introduces the warrior priests, the black cloaked baddies (wh</span>
  <span id="freeText9379154475706709208" style="display:none">Unlike <a href="http://ift.tt/1nl9iV8" rel="nofollow noopener">my ambivalence to Tenaka Khan</a>, I very much liked the eponymous Waylander (aka Dakeyras) as an imperfect hero (he's not quite the anti-hero, though he skirts that line nicely). Also, I enjoy the fact that I get to use "eponymous" in a review; happens far too rarely.<br /><br />When I first started <u>Waylander (Drenai Saga, #3)</u>, it took me a while before I realized that I was reading a prequel to the two books (<a href="http://email.ifttt.com/wf/click?upn=jGHDfwvrKDxaofcg5GVulg9CQ9akl7TWey9wviWZQJM-3D_bM0v-2Fecqq1kET4-2B3AH3g8cUy7KuK0lvX75Kf8LifO-2BBpV0eHEe-2BfWsH-2BqLuRjd1udgb1fJSnj1Y4LFAfCBFds-2FpTiJBSL-2FrLqfRLjSZXlqb8yW1qCCrzqb-2Fgnv2fXBpc88jvcEzZsGgwhQxQ-2FdvpJjomFs6-2BifL0gdNnkTBE8vCIMTnXSllI3SLqR4y6NGRvGleoEVwxbFEVtQ6GgYXnpHgzZ9hZfXC215LWsqdZHlrY4DBy0ECyA0N0eJUv7wzRPr6R0TMh-2FAOabTbyN6S6kBk9f7QSn4df2ITEQUjRls4Ts-2FSZ7heCzYI6TZGh0IG3GYqg9dHgErFKesjOxkAY5ho7dK4Ef5uyUuSueACa34FQxsk6rueC7xMr3sW9-2BoYh0XXDpwVeF-2F2S9vuiZcp0bg-3D-3D" rel="nofollow noopener">#1</a>, <a href="http://ift.tt/1nl9iV8" rel="nofollow noopener">#2</a>) that had come before. It introduces the warrior priests, the black cloaked baddies (who only appeared <a href="http://ift.tt/1nl9iV8" rel="nofollow noopener">in book #2</a>), plans to build Dros Delnoch that features prominently in <a href="http://ift.tt/1iWMyE8" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a> and <a href="http://ift.tt/1nl9iV8" rel="nofollow noopener">even has furries (though not terribly kawaii)</a>.<br /><br />While others will tell you that this book centers around questions of redemption, I found this novel to center around the question, "Can one be brave enough to lose oneself to love a second time in life?" After all, it was the elimination of Waylander's first loves that started him down his path, and it <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[takes a second round of love <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> to remove him from that path and return him to his original state.<br /><br />And to that end, I am more pleased with how <a href="http://ift.tt/1nl9iV8" rel="nofollow noopener">Gemmel wrote the male-female interaction in this novel</a>. While still not ideal, Daynal has her own opinions and isn't shy about stating them. Some might call this nagging, but I simply view it as someone who isn't a doormat. Glad to see <a href="http://ift.tt/1nl9iV8" rel="nofollow noopener">things are improving</a>.<br /><br />As said by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450108906?book_show_action=true&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">reviewer Anders</a>:<br /><blockquote>It has a fair amount of resemblance to other Drenai books I have read, but it is conveyed in such a way here, that it only serves to strengthen the overall story and plot.</blockquote><br /><br />Not much more I can add to that except to say that you should read this. Right now. Without hesitation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9379154475706709208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<ul>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1468518.White_Knight_Black_Swan"><img alt="White Knight, Black Swan" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1183914407l/1468518._SY160_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IY0BtyhKiHMuZ8qADuUedu1qpHHvfzXRPNx3ss0WUMIdhgl5E7XIZdOZkXTHRTy3nvQjXBXtnGTxFyUnimJ46A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YrZS2QjU9GI42eV6s+KvGwiPgM//cZiITfiUqSWpKjpevVoXMyu0dMUnvo56Qo3aexEH4gXjMT2AM8Y8Yt0CEA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1586422407270139247">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sel</span>
  <span id="freeText1586422407270139247" style="display:none">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sell worldwide.</span>

An ancient prophecy foretold that Skilgannon would return in his people\'s darkest hour. To most, this was a foolish hope. But not so to Landis Kan. Having found Skilgannon\'s ancient tomb, he gathers up the bones and peforms the mystic ritual.\n\nBut the reborn hero is an enigma: a young man whose warrior skills are blunted and whose memories are fragmented. This Skilgannon is a man out of time, Marooned in a world as strange to him as a dream, remote from all he knew and loved. Or nearly all. Before bringing back Skilgannon, Landis Kan had experimented upon other bone fragments found in the hero\'s tomb. That ritual resulted in a surly giant who possessed astounding strength but no memories. To Kan, he is a dangerous failure. To Skilgannon, this giant represents their last hope.\n\nAs ageless evil threatens to drown the Drenai lands in blood, two legendary heroes will once again lead the way to freedom.<\/span>\n  <a
